<div id="review_1088893379" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088893379" />
    <a title="Anirudh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh"><img alt="Anirudh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359010972p2/16686132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1088893379?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anirudh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anirudh" href="/user/show/16686132-anirudh">Anirudh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788125931867" href="/book/show/12904262-freedom-at-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1088893379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12471085149177599343">It is rare for me to read a non fiction. But fortunately I chose a good book to read. <br/><br/>Freedom at midnight, captures India on two occasions. One, her independence, one of the best moments in her history. Two, the partition, probably the worst time in her history. <br/><br/><b>Narration</b>:- The author has a distinct advantage which ironically is a disadvantage as well. He gets an outside perspective of India, allowing him to criticise without having to feel obligated to justify any act or man. It is also a disad</span>
  <span id="freeText12471085149177599343" style="display:none">It is rare for me to read a non fiction. But fortunately I chose a good book to read. <br /><br />Freedom at midnight, captures India on two occasions. One, her independence, one of the best moments in her history. Two, the partition, probably the worst time in her history. <br /><br /><b>Narration</b>:- The author has a distinct advantage which ironically is a disadvantage as well. He gets an outside perspective of India, allowing him to criticise without having to feel obligated to justify any act or man. It is also a disadvantage because he ends up making several assumtions which are incorrect. <br /><br />For the most part the narration is very engaging, urging the readers to read on. When it is not engaging however, it is not so because bad narration but because the subject becomes so brutal and horrifying. Even after 60 odd years, the recollection of some of the events is truly sickening, even to those of my generation who have never experienced the anguish the men and women at that time suffered. <br /><br /><b>Perspective</b> The perspective of this book is both fascinating and appalling. The author does not hesitate to criticise the Maharajas of India and Indian national leaders. However he also often paints Mountbattion in a favourable light. The one Englishman who thought only the good of India and guided her journey. Which is anything but true. Perhaps because Mountbatton is one of the main source of this book, he has attained a status of a man who made everything possible without making any mistakes. <br /><br />The author however, succeeds because of the little incidents he manages to present in an engaging way. For example, how the line of partition was actually drawn and by whom. I can say with utmost certainty that no text book contains this information and nor will it. When reading about these little things, one begins to understand more about the partition than what is generally understood. <br /><br />However the author does make several incorrect claims. He makes references to two nation theory which has already been set aside as inaccurate. The British also come off as a great set of people. A sane voice amidst the chaos of religious clashes. However the author cleverly forgets how they flared the differences between religions in India when it suited them. The partition of Bengal, the famine of Bengal hardly make an appearance. He also makes references to the 'Aryan Invasion Theory' which has been proven incorrect more than once. <br /><br />Overall, it is a book that is worth reading. Recommended to people who love history. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12471085149177599343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText335183847518775134" style="display:none">There are enough reviews about the content of this book. I will provide my reactions<br /><br />1. I usually do not buy books, preferring to borrow from a library. I took this one from the library, but after reading it I ordered a copy for myself.<br />2. It is a history book, encapsulating the one year in which India was made, unmade, and then remade. If my history books had been written by La pierre and Collins, I would have never taken up engineering<br />3. Painstaking research usually results in unreadable material. But this one is different.     <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1469803-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293658827p2/1469803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/31383932?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/1469803-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

  <span id="freeText4332558580157552120" style="display:none">I see that the header here has failed to note that this book was written by a team of authors: Dominique Lapierre and Larry Collins. These authors are simply brilliant and have collaberated on a number of stunning historical books about key moments in history, among them, "Is Paris Burning" &amp; "O Jerusalem". This volume is about the struggle for liberation from British rule in India. I HIGHLY recommend it to anyone interested in the subject. Lapierre &amp; Collins are terrific writers and their works are riveting, well-paced and packed with interesting information and history. If you like history but not the druggery of reading blah blah boring writers, THESE are the historians for you. Brilliant books!</span>

  <span id="freeText418743463804810272" style="display:none">I'm leaving for India, and this book was recommended to me. Trains arrived in Indian stations with compartments full of dead and maimed passengers, blood flowing from compartments. Each side experienced atrocities. How did I not know any of this?</span>

<div id="review_1846399739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846399739" />
    <a title="Ankit Mishra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56344667-ankit-mishra"><img alt="Ankit Mishra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483094539p2/56344667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1846399739?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ankit Mishra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ankit Mishra" href="/user/show/56344667-ankit-mishra">Ankit Mishra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846399739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15314492300354595006">The composition of this book is such that you won't find it difficult to read through the pages, and the authors have weaved it with simple, yet strong literature. The way they have covered the whole period of Independence in over 650 pages is commendable, considering the fact that they have covered almost all the important events. <br/><br/>The book boasts of an exhaustive research done in the library of Mountbatten, over dinners and back in India, which gives an impression that the book is true to the e</span>
  <span id="freeText15314492300354595006" style="display:none">The composition of this book is such that you won't find it difficult to read through the pages, and the authors have weaved it with simple, yet strong literature. The way they have covered the whole period of Independence in over 650 pages is commendable, considering the fact that they have covered almost all the important events. <br /><br />The book boasts of an exhaustive research done in the library of Mountbatten, over dinners and back in India, which gives an impression that the book is true to the events and emotions of the era. <br /><br />But sadly, this is a book that tries to justify Britain's occupancy of India, trying to put with an utmost subtlety that the Britishers had no bad intentions and they did nothing but help India grow and become a better nation.<br /><br />As you read, you'll find a great deal is written about Mahatma Gandhi, the "dejected bird" of Mountbatten, Nehru, the handsome Indian who is incredibly fascinated by the Mountbattens, Jinnah, the only guy who is shown in the bad light, and Patel, well... Let's just say he exists. <br /><br />The book is just a manuscript to put forth Britain as the wise and better, quoting Rudyard Kipling, who says that Indians better be ruled by Britishers, and heavily quoting Churchill, who has been depicted as a "guy too important to be in a book on India". <br /><br />At one point, the book talks of "millions of cattle who ate all the food that could have used to feed the Indian masses" but ignorantly decides to skip the tale of the famines caused by the Raj, that killed more Indians than Jews killed by Hitler. <br /><br />The "rich indulgence of Indian kings" has been quoted in great detail, while the atrocities on Indian wealth and citizens by the British have been ignored. <br /><br />The sad demise of young Britishers who died in India has been subjected to all the love, but not a drop of ink been wasted for the millions of Indians, who died pleasing their "memsahibs".<br /><br />The lives of the young British officials stands as an example, enduring the harsh weather, and the problems of the "poor country". The authors, very blatantly quote that "a land of 83% illiterates got independent, but they forget to quote that it was them, who ruled these masses for 200 years, which makes them solely responsible for everything, right(a few) or wrong. <br /><br />A book written only to make you like the British Raj, making Mountbatten the hero of all this, being equally praised by the British and Indians. <br /><br />The book, though very well written, fails to provide the real picture of the struggle and suffering that Indians went through and tries to, through the power of the pen, make everything right what the Britishers did wrong.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15314492300354595006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143284230" />
    <a title="Addy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60843405-addy"><img alt="Addy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513015029p2/60843405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143284230?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Addy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Addy" href="/user/show/60843405-addy">Addy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60843405-addy?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143284230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7945550889537453740">So, I finally successfully moved out of my reading 'comfort zone' and actually finished a non fiction book(despite finishing 4 other fiction novels since I started this). And the best part is I absolutely loved it. <br/><br/>This book is imo, a must read for each and every Indian and Pakistani to actually understand in detail what exactly happened during those tumultuous times in an unbiased manner through the eyes of the person who was at its epicentre. <br/><br/>Now, I'm not gonna waste too much space on what my </span>
  <span id="freeText7945550889537453740" style="display:none">So, I finally successfully moved out of my reading 'comfort zone' and actually finished a non fiction book(despite finishing 4 other fiction novels since I started this). And the best part is I absolutely loved it. <br /><br />This book is imo, a must read for each and every Indian and Pakistani to actually understand in detail what exactly happened during those tumultuous times in an unbiased manner through the eyes of the person who was at its epicentre. <br /><br />Now, I'm not gonna waste too much space on what my views about Mountbatten, Gandhi, Nehru, Jinnah or Nathu Ram Godse were/are but I can say with some conviction that those views will be much more informed now than they were before reading this book. <br /><br />Be it Clement Attlee's persistence in persuading Mountbatten to take up the most difficult job of becoming The Raj's last Viceroy; Mountbatten's own apprehensions, his numerous tete-a-tetes with Jinnah, Gandhi, Nehru, Patel; the division of Punjab by Radcliffe's pencil on a map, the inevitable horrors on both sides of the new border; the planning and execution of Gandhi's execution - everything was described in so much detail backed by impeccable research and most importantly, the story telling was top notch. Infact, it picks up the pace of a proper thriller once the assassination part kicks in. <br /><br />Think this is one book which every kid in the subcontinent should read before he finishes high school. Glad that I've read it now, even if, 15 years too late. <br /><br />5/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7945550889537453740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_506199341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/506199341" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54752-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184819140p2/54752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/506199341?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/54752-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer506199341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8644304528977685978">Brilliantly reported and written, this 1975 nonfiction book tells the story of the year India became an independent nation and the new nation of Pakistan was created. It covers all of 1947 and about a month of 1948, ending with the assassination of Mahatma Gandhi.<br/>Gandhi is, of course, a central character. Not having ever seen the movie and not having ever read a book about Gandhi, I learned a lot about him. He was certainly one of the giants of the 20th century.<br/>Among the other central characters</span>
  <span id="freeText8644304528977685978" style="display:none">Brilliantly reported and written, this 1975 nonfiction book tells the story of the year India became an independent nation and the new nation of Pakistan was created. It covers all of 1947 and about a month of 1948, ending with the assassination of Mahatma Gandhi.<br />Gandhi is, of course, a central character. Not having ever seen the movie and not having ever read a book about Gandhi, I learned a lot about him. He was certainly one of the giants of the 20th century.<br />Among the other central characters are Lord Louis and Lady Edwina Mountbatten, the reluctant last viceroy and last vicereine of India. Prime Minister Clement Atlee prevailed upon Mountbatten to superintend the end of Great Britain's reign in India, and Mountbatten's cousin the king added his support. <br />As badly as things turned out, it's hard to imagine anyone filling the role nearly as well as Mountbatten did. It speaks of the respect he won in a short time that he was asked to stay on as governor general of India. And although that was a largely ceremonial title, the government's leaders asked him to secretly take on almost dictatorial powers when the crisis came.<br />Edwina Mountbatten was as hard-working and courageous as her husband, and she was more of a people person. (Lord Mountbatten could be a bit of a bully.) As the authors put it, "She could preside over a formal banquet in a diamond tiara one night and minister with skill and compassion to cholera victims in a fetid slum the next morning."<br />It's hard to imagine a new government starting out with greater difficulty than India did in the summer and fall of 1947. In the first six weeks of independence, half as many people died violent deaths in India and Pakistan as the number of all the Americans who died in all of World War II. And the savagery that accompanied the deaths was horrifying -- Moslems at the hands of Hindus and Sikhs; Hindus and Sikhs at the hands of Moslems. <br />The chapter that describes that period, "Our People Have Gone Mad," is the most depressing chapter I can remember reading in any book.<br />The detail of the reporting in "Freedom at Midnight" is astonishing. The writing is superb.<br />Here's an especially evocative excerpt, from Page 206, with Jawarharlal Nehru and Mahatma Gandhi traveling together as independence neared and they felt the weight of all India on their shoulders:<br /><br />"Eyes straight ahead, his usually expressive face a mask, Nehru rode for a long time in silence, pondering, perhaps, what future the sights they had witnessed portended for the India he would soon be called upon to govern. Then, slowly, tenderly, as though to expiate with his gentle touch the pain he had caused him, he began to massage the callused feet of the sleeping man to whom he had devoted so much of his life.<br />"At sunset, Gandhi awoke. From each side of their speeding car, the broad fields of sugar cane, wheat, paddy, flat as a man's hand, ran down to a horizon so distant that it might seem the edge of the world. A fine haze stood above the vast plain filtering through its screen the last roseate glow of the sinking sun. It was the cow-dust hour, an hour as ancient, as unforgettable as India itself. From a thousand, tens of thousands of mud-brick huts speckling the great Punjab plain it came, the smoke of India's mealtime fires. Everywhere, squatting on their haunches, faded saris clutched to their shoulders, bangles clanking on their bare arms, the women tended those fires, fussing over the chapaties and channa they were cooking, stoking them with the found flat patties of dried dung that fueled them, the last of the many gifts of India's sacred cows. The mantle of Indian night, the smoke from those numberless cow-dung fires drifting through the evening sky, permeating it with the distinctive pungent smell that was the body odor of Mother India."</span>
  <a data-text-id="8644304528977685978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1791560094" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791560094" />
    <a title="Krish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11962530-krish"><img alt="Krish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545985113p2/11962530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1791560094?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krish" href="/user/show/11962530-krish">Krish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1791560094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3043342271473530009">This is an important book that reveals the fine-grained details that transpired during the transition of India from the British raj to an independent one. Like most historical non-fiction books, it inevitably suffers from biases, but that does not discount many of the facts presented. However one chooses to look at the events that unfolded, this book will reveal the highly complex and random nature of the process of India's freedom and the country's administration immediately thereafter. Some kn</span>
  <span id="freeText3043342271473530009" style="display:none">This is an important book that reveals the fine-grained details that transpired during the transition of India from the British raj to an independent one. Like most historical non-fiction books, it inevitably suffers from biases, but that does not discount many of the facts presented. However one chooses to look at the events that unfolded, this book will reveal the highly complex and random nature of the process of India's freedom and the country's administration immediately thereafter. Some knowledge and/or insights I acquired from this book:<br /><br />1) Mountbatten and Britain's task of transfer of power was a thanklessly complex one. Whether it was carried out in the best manner possible or not, the consequences had to be horrible for a large number of people. Even with the benefit of hindsight, one (or at least myself) can not predict whether it was right to:<br />a) expedite the process of power transfer,<br />b) not keep India undivided, and<br />c) help India get Kashmir, rather than let it remain independent or be taken by force by Pakistan.<br /><br />2) Nehru, Patel and other Indian leaders were understandably inexperienced in administration. If not for Britain's existing military organizations and the British administration's advice, the riots that plagued the aftermath of the partition might have had even more disastrous consequences than they did in actuality.<br /><br />3) Gandhi's role in quelling riots in Noakhali, Calcutta and Delhi was immense. If not for his peculiar obstinacy and saint-like adherence to principles of non-violence, many more innocent lives would have ended. At the same time, one wonders whether he unwittingly did sympathize with Muslim lives more than Hindu lives that led to his own demise as well as the anti-Muslim sentiment that got accentuated among extremist Hindus.<br /><br />4) Given the socialist welfare ideals of Nehru, the world lost a big opportunity to test the efficacy of decentralized administration the way Gandhi imagined for India. No top administrative official in India worked towards an India of self-sufficient villages with little dependence on materialism and a strong base in spiritual well-being. Maybe this is never practically possible, but I wish that a true believer in the ideals of Gandhi and not just the man himself had led the nation and tested his theory.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3043342271473530009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_739574749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739574749" />
    <a title="S.Ach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/233507-s-ach"><img alt="S.Ach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515914630p2/233507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739574749?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.Ach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.Ach" href="/user/show/233507-s-ach">S.Ach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788125931645" href="/book/show/6718481-freedom-at-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233507-s-ach?shelf=ind-pak-partition">ind-pak-partition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233507-s-ach?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233507-s-ach?shelf=india">india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/233507-s-ach?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739574749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11478409317293188341">Just few days after, India officially got independence, the two spearheads of then Indian politics, Jawaharlal Nehru and Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, visited the outgoing Viceroy Lord Mountbatten, and requested him to take back his previous charge. Reason - they felt incapable of handling the horrendous situation partition had presented before them. "Take back the power of India, else there won't be any India," they pleaded.<br/>Mountbatten obliged and, sort-of staying in background, administered in mil</span>
  <span id="freeText11478409317293188341" style="display:none">Just few days after, India officially got independence, the two spearheads of then Indian politics, Jawaharlal Nehru and Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, visited the outgoing Viceroy Lord Mountbatten, and requested him to take back his previous charge. Reason - they felt incapable of handling the horrendous situation partition had presented before them. "Take back the power of India, else there won't be any India," they pleaded.<br />Mountbatten obliged and, sort-of staying in background, administered in military precision the smooth exodus of Indian Muslims and newly formed Pakistan's non-Muslims.<br /><br />Thus, the book has brought forward the stark reality behind India's Freedom from the colonial rule. In that course, of course the book feels somehow slanted towards eulogizing Lord Mountbatten, but show me a history book that is not biased at all.<br /><br />The book describes in vibrant colour and in fiction-like tone few days before ( from the day the Lord Mountbatten took the office) to the funeral day of the father of the Nation. The amount of research that has gone through the book is reflected in every page. The book has been written in a way as if the author were the eye-witness of all the incidents, and now the readers are.<br /><br />The horror of partition was so animated in the book, you would flinch with revulsion. The plot of assassinating the Mahatma would make you restless. The struggle and stubbornness of political leaders to get their objectives would make you wonder, "Was the freedom really worth it?" 40s is the most important period in Indian history and the 40's India comes alive in every sentence of this book. The socio-economic conditions, the religious mindsets, the convoluted politics - you live the fight for freedom yourself throught this book. I am sure, after reading this book, you would look at our famous national leaders in a different light than before.<br /><br />I have not read many books on Indian independence ( if you count the boring text books of school) to judge whether this is the best book ever written on the subject. But, undoubtedly, this one is the best history book I have ever read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11478409317293188341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_405319873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/405319873" />
    <a title="Laini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1912701-laini"><img alt="Laini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352054577p2/1912701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/405319873?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laini" href="/user/show/1912701-laini">Laini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780671220884" href="/book/show/3322437-freedom-at-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1912701-laini?shelf=cultural-glimpses">cultural-glimpses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1912701-laini?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1912701-laini?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1912701-laini?shelf=it-really-happened">it-really-happened</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer405319873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer290065898246704505">A fascinating book. <br/><br/>I knew that India and Pakistan had been partitioned, but I didn't know all the details of what happened and when. And it explains many cultural nuances with which I was not familiar. <br/><br/>I didn't realize that part of the reason that Hindus hate Muslims so much is because many Muslims took up that religion because they were Hindu Untouchables who didn't want to wait for the next life to have a little say-so in what happened to them. The Hindus always considered Muslims unclean bec</span>
  <span id="freeText290065898246704505" style="display:none">A fascinating book. <br /><br />I knew that India and Pakistan had been partitioned, but I didn't know all the details of what happened and when. And it explains many cultural nuances with which I was not familiar. <br /><br />I didn't realize that part of the reason that Hindus hate Muslims so much is because many Muslims took up that religion because they were Hindu Untouchables who didn't want to wait for the next life to have a little say-so in what happened to them. The Hindus always considered Muslims unclean because of this. <br /><br />The violence that occurred because of partition (from all sides) was a pre-cursor to what we in the modern day associate with places like Bosnia and Croatia, on a more giant scale because of the massive population.<br /><br />Something I did not expect to occur when reading the book was to lose respect for Gandhi. But I did. While liberated in his views on women in some respects, others (like his views on rape-- just lie back and take it, ladies. Or overpopulation...don't use birth control. Just do like me and not have sex) were ludicrous. And I was actually pulling for the Muslims to have their own country. If you can't play well together, something else has to happen, and the Muslims were obviously underrepresented enough to know what would happen when the English pulled out. It did. <br /><br />I was not familiar with Jinnah before reading the book, but gained a great deal of respect for him. Except for not allowing his personal plane to transport his Muslim countrymen out of harm's way while he was dying. Evidently, in his last days, he became more bitter and selfish. But he had a singularity of purpose I found admirable. And he got his homeland. <br /><br />And while the authors definitely adore Mountbatten, I did learn more about him and about the Raj rule than I knew previously. <br /><br />This book has given me a new window into Indian and Pakistani culture that has really been educational and eye-opening. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="290065898246704505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ajit Dharmik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1300335-ajit-dharmik"><img alt="Ajit Dharmik" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26364397?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ajit Dharmik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ajit Dharmik" href="/user/show/1300335-ajit-dharmik">Ajit Dharmik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780006388517" href="/book/show/884142.Freedom_at_Midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1300335-ajit-dharmik?shelf=history">history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26364397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2130291613309541421">For all those interested in the events surrounding India's independence, creation of Pakistan, and the holocaust that followed, this is a good read. The authors have done a great job describing the political posturing preceding 15th August 1947, how Hindus & Sikhs on one side and Muslims massacred each other, providing all the gory details. <br/><br/>I especially liked the way they described how ordinary Indians celebrated 15th August 1947. I can almost see myself near Connaught Place in New Delhi, celebr</span>
  <span id="freeText2130291613309541421" style="display:none">For all those interested in the events surrounding India's independence, creation of Pakistan, and the holocaust that followed, this is a good read. The authors have done a great job describing the political posturing preceding 15th August 1947, how Hindus &amp; Sikhs on one side and Muslims massacred each other, providing all the gory details. <br /><br />I especially liked the way they described how ordinary Indians celebrated 15th August 1947. I can almost see myself near Connaught Place in New Delhi, celebrating my country's new-found freedom.<br /><br />However, one thing I didn't quite understand was the authors' keeping Mountbatten on a pedestal. According to them, Mountbatten could do no wrong, was a perfect Governor General, while Nehru and Sardar Patel were mere schools boys in comparison. This pro-Mountbatten bend robs this narrative of some objectivity and leads me to give 3 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2130291613309541421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KiN2WQFVGQGc/KSqmyhtRNxXzY+lC4Mjt1JUbxXVFSfKPHeeTTZitNsynU6Rdu4RY0VAvipOGyHlNWZtNOUDkw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_124429'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/124429.The_Last_Mughal?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Last Mughal: The Fall of a Dynasty: Delhi, 1857<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/60159.William_Dalrymple?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">William Dalrymple<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.16 avg rating &mdash; 6,587 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2006\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5851934566794501172\">On a hazy November afternoon in Rangoon, 1862, a shrouded corpse was escorted by a small group of British soldiers to an anonymous grave in a prison enclosure. As the British Commissioner in charge insisted, “No vestige will remain to distinguish whe<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5851934566794501172\" style=\"display:none\">On a hazy November afternoon in Rangoon, 1862, a shrouded corpse was escorted by a small group of British soldiers to an anonymous grave in a prison enclosure. As the British Commissioner in charge insisted, “No vestige will remain to distinguish where the last of the Great Moghuls rests.” Bahadur Shah Zafar II, the last Mughal Emperor, was a mystic, an accomplished poet and a skilled calligrapher. But while his Mughal ancestors had controlled most of India, the aged Zafar was king in name only. Deprived of real political power by the East India Company, he nevertheless succeeded in creating a court of great brilliance, and presided over one of the great cultural renaissances of Indian history.Then, in 1857, Zafar gave his blessing to a rebellion among the Company’s own Indian troops, thereby transforming an army mutiny into the largest uprising any empire had to face in the entire course of the nineteenth century. The Siege of Delhi was the Raj’s Stalingrad: one of the most horrific events in the history of Empire, in which thousands on both sides died. And when the British took the city—securing their hold on the subcontinent for the next ninety years—tens of thousands more Indians were executed, including all but two of Zafar’s sixteen sons. By the end of the four-month siege, Delhi was reduced to a battered, empty ruin, and Zafar was sentenced to exile in Burma. There he died, the last Mughal ruler in a line that stretched back to the sixteenth century.Award-winning historian and travel writer William Dalrymple shapes his powerful retelling of this fateful course of events from groundbreaking material: previously unexamined Urdu and Persian manuscripts that include Indian eyewitness accounts and records of the Delhi courts, police and administration during the siege. The Last Mughal is a revelatory work—the first to present the Indian perspective on the fall of Delhi—and has as its heart both the dazzling capital personified by Zafar and the stories of the individuals tragically caught up in one of the bloodiest upheavals in history.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5851934566794501172\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer wtrSignedOut\' id=\'18_book_124429\'>\n<div class=\'wtrUp wtrLeft\'>\n<form action=\"/shelf/add_to_shelf\" <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/290376.Indira"><img alt="Indira: The Life of Indira Nehru Gandhi" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1387701553l/290376._SX98_.jpg" />

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_290376'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/290376.Indira?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Indira: The Life of Indira Nehru Gandhi<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/8248.Katherine_Frank?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Katherine Frank<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\" title=\"really liked it\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\">really liked it<\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 4.00 avg rating &mdash; 1,984 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2001\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer10831507635131127809\">On the morning of October 31, 1984, as she walked through her garden, smiling, with hands raised and palms pressed together in the traditional Indian namaste greeting, Indira Nehru Gandhi was assassinated by her own bodyguards. She died as she had li<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10831507635131127809\" style=\"display:none\">On the morning of October 31, 1984, as she walked through her garden, smiling, with hands raised and palms pressed together in the traditional Indian namaste greeting, Indira Nehru Gandhi was assassinated by her own bodyguards. She died as she had lived, surrounded by men, yet isolated. It was a violent end to a life of epic drama. Here is the first popular biography of one of the world\'s most influential leaders, India\'s third prime minister. Brought up during an era that saw the rise of Indian nationalism, Indira was raised to be what her father, Jawaharlal Nehru, called &quot;a child of revolution&quot; - destined to play a political role in the creation and governing of an independent India. Despite her early reluctance to embrace this role, Indira eventually presided over a huge, complex, religiously riven, and male-dominated country. She was born to a wealthy, westernized family, but she had a gift for connecting with the poor of the countryside and the urban slums, the illiterate, the dispossessed - so much so that &quot;Indira is India&quot; became a familiar slogan. Throughout childhood, love, marriage, imprisonment, motherhood, and a sequence of personal and family tragedies, her personal hopes and desires were continually subsumed by the historical and political imperatives of her country. In this beautifully written book, the acclaimed biographer Katherine Frank draws on unpublished sources and more than a hundred interviews to create a rich, balanced portrait. INDIRA captures in full color the personal and political fate of the leader of the world\'s largest democracy - the woman who played a dominant role in the history of the twentieth century and who, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32618967-an-era-of-darkness"><img alt="An Era of Darkness: The British Empire in India" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1476625646l/32618967._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_32618967'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32618967-an-era-of-darkness?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">An Era of Darkness: The British Empire in India<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17287.Shashi_Tharoor?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Shashi Tharoor<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.16 avg rating &mdash; 7,165 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2016\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer1790274989297825891\">In 1930, the American historian and philosopher Will Durant wrote that Britain’s ‘conscious and deliberate bleeding of India… [was the] greatest crime in all history’. He was not the only one to denounce the rapacity and cruelty of British rule, and <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1790274989297825891\" style=\"display:none\">In 1930, the American historian and philosopher Will Durant wrote that Britain’s ‘conscious and deliberate bleeding of India… [was the] greatest crime in all history’. He was not the only one to denounce the rapacity and cruelty of British rule, and his assessment was not exaggerated. Almost thirty-five million Indians died because of acts of commission and omission by the British—in famines, epidemics, communal riots and wholesale slaughter like the reprisal killings after the 1857 War of Independence and the Amritsar massacre of 1919. \n\nBesides the deaths of Indians, British rule impoverished India in a manner that beggars belief. When the East India Company took control of the country, in the chaos that ensued after the collapse of the Mughal empire, India’s share of world GDP was 23 per cent. When the British left it was just above 3 per cent. \n\nThe British empire in India began with the East India Company, incorporated in 1600, by royal charter of Her Majesty Queen Elizabeth I, to trade in silk, spices and other profitable Indian commodities. Within a century and a half, the Company had become a power to reckon with in India. In 1757, under the command of Robert Clive, Company forces defeated the ruling Nawab Siraj-ud-Daula of Bengal at Plassey, through a combination of superior artillery and even more superior chicanery. A few years later, the young and weakened Mughal emperor, Shah Alam II, was browbeaten into issuing an edict that replaced his own revenue officials with the Company’s representatives. Over the next several decades, the East India Company, backed by the British government, extended its control over most of India, ruling with a combination of extortion, double-dealing, and outright corruption backed by violence and superior force. This state of affairs continued until 1857, when large numbers of the Company’s Indian soldiers spearheaded the first major rebellion against colonial rule. After the rebels were defeated, the British Crown took over power and ruled the country ostensibly more benignly until 1947, when India won independence. \n\nIn this explosive book, bestselling author Shashi Tharoor reveals with acuity, impeccable research, and trademark wit, just how disastrous British rule was for India. Besides examining the many ways in which the colonizers exploited India, ranging from the drain of national resources to Britain, the destruction of the Indian textile, steel-making and shipping industries, and the negative transformation of agriculture, he demolishes the arguments of Western and Indian apologists for Empire on the supposed benefits of British rule, including democracy and political freedom, the rule of law, and the railways.\n \nThe few unarguable benefits—the English language, tea, and cricket—were never actually intended for the benefit of the colonized but introduced to serve the interests of the colonizers. Brilliantly narrated and passionately argued, An Era of Darkness will serve to correct many misconceptions about one of the most contested periods of Indian history.<\/span>\n  <a The result is a country that, while managing incredible economic growth, has also begun to fully inhabit its role on the world political stage. In this far-ranging look at the central ideas that have shaped this young nation, Infosys cofounder Nandan Nilekani offers a definitive and original interpretation of the country\'s past, present, and future. India\'s future rests on more than simply economic growth; it also depends on reform and innovation in all sectors of public life. Imagining India traces the efforts of the country\'s past and present leaders as they work to develop new frameworks that suit India\'s specific characteristics and challenges. Imagining India charts the ideas that are crucial to India\'s current infrastructure revolution and quest for universal literacy, urbanization, and unification; maps the ideological battlegrounds of caste, higher education, and labor reform; and argues that only a safety net of ideas from social security to public health to the environment can transcend political agendas and safeguard India\'s economic future. As a cofounder of Infosys, a global leader in information technology, Nandan Nilekani has actively participated in the company\'s rise in the last fifteen years. In Imagining India, he uses the global experience and understanding he has gained at Infosys as a springboard from which to discuss the future of India and its role as a global citizen and emerging economic giant. A fascinating window into the future of India, Imagining India engages with the central ideas and challenges that face the country from within and as a part of the global economy and charts a new way       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/35332.Larry_Collins">About Larry Collins</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/35332.Larry_Collins"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1251800469p3/35332.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/35332.Larry_Collins">Larry Collins
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
138
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5027566327562677250">Born in West Hartford, Connecticut, he was educated at the Loomis Chaffee Institute in Windsor, Connecticut, and graduated from Yale as a BA in 1951. He worked in the advertising department of Procter and Gamble, in Cincinnati, Ohio, before being conscripted into the US Army. While serving in the public affairs office of the Allied Headquarters in Paris, from 1953-1955, he met Dominique Lapierre w</span>
  <span id="freeText5027566327562677250" style="display:none">Born in West Hartford, Connecticut, he was educated at the Loomis Chaffee Institute in Windsor, Connecticut, and graduated from Yale as a BA in 1951. He worked in the advertising department of Procter and Gamble, in Cincinnati, Ohio, before being conscripted into the US Army. While serving in the public affairs office of the Allied Headquarters in Paris, from 1953-1955, he met Dominique Lapierre with whom he would write several best-sellers over 43 years.<br /><br />He went back to Procter and Gamble and became the products manager of the new foods division in 1955. Disillusioned with commerce, he took to journalism and joined the Paris bureau of United Press International in 1956, and became the news editor in Rome in the following year, and later the MidEast bureau chief in Beirut.<br /><br />In 1959, he joined Newsweek as Middle East editor, based in New York. He became the Paris bureau chief in 1961, where he would work until 1964, until he switched to writing books.<br /><br />In 1965, Collins and Lapierre published their first joint work, Is Paris Burning? (in French Paris brûle-t-il?), a tale of Nazi occupation of the French capital during World War II and Hitler's plans to destroy Paris should it fall into the hands of the Allies. The book was an instant success and was made into a movie in 1966 by director René Clément, starring Kirk Douglas, Glenn Ford and Alain Delon.<br /><br />In 1967, they co-authored Or I'll Dress you in Mourning about the Spanish bullfighter Manuel Benítez El Cordobés.<br /><br />In 1972, after five years' research and interviews, they published O Jerusalem! about the birth of Israel in 1948, turned into a movie by Elie Chouraqui.<br /><br />In 1975, they published Freedom at Midnight, a story of the Indian Independence in 1947, and the subsequent assassination of Mahatma Gandhi in 1948. It is said they spent $300,000 researching and still emerged wealthy.<br /><br />The duo published their first fictional work, The Fifth Horseman, in 1981. It describes a terrorist attack on New York masterminded by Libya's Colonel Gaddafi. The book had such a shocking effect that the French President cancelled the sale of nuclear reactors to Libya, even though it was meant for peaceful purposes. Paramount Pictures, which was planning a film based on the book, dropped the idea in fear that fanatics would emulate the scenario in real life.<br /><br />In 1985, Collins authored Fall From Grace (without Lapierre) about a woman agent sent into occupied France who realizes she may be betrayed by her British masters if necessary. He also wrote Maze: A Novel (1989), Black Eagles (1995), Le Jour Du Miracle: D-Day Paris (1994) and Tomorrow Belongs To Us (1998). Shortly before his death, he collaborated with Lapierre on Is New York Burning? (2005), a novel mixing fictional characters and real-life figures that speculates about a terrorist attack on New York City.<br /><br />In 2005, while working from his home in the south of France on a book on the Middle East, Collins died of a sudden cerebral haemorrhage.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5027566327562677250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
